         [103]
        </a>
       </sup>
       One estimate suggests that, given the turnover rate inferred from the apparent ~0.5 Gyr maximum age of Europa's surface ice, subduction of radiolytically generated oxidizing species might well lead to oceanic free oxygen concentrations that are comparable to those in terrestrial deep oceans.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ChemDisequilib_110-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ChemDisequilib-110">
         [104]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The molecular hydrogen that escapes Europa's gravity, along with atomic and molecular oxygen, forms a
       <a href="/wiki/Gas_torus" title="Gas torus">
        gas torus
       </a>
       in the vicinity of Europa's orbit around Jupiter. This "neutral cloud" has been detected by both the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Cassini%E2%80%93Huygens" title="Cassini–Huygens">
         Cassini
        </a>
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        Galileo
       </i>
       spacecraft, and has a greater content (number of atoms and molecules) than the neutral cloud surrounding Jupiter's inner moon
       <a href="/wiki/Io_(moon)" title="Io (moon)">
        Io
       </a>
       . Models predict that almost every atom or molecule in Europa's torus is eventually ionized, thus providing a source to Jupiter's magnetospheric plasma.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Smyth2006_111-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Smyth2006-111">
         [105]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Exploration">
        Exploration
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Europa_(moon)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Exploration">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:224px;max-width:224px">
        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px">
         <div class="thumbimage">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pioneer_10_-_p102b.jpg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="209" data-file-width="206" height="223" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6e/Pioneer_10_-_p102b.jpg" width="220"/>
          </a>
         </div>
         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
          <a href="/wiki/Pioneer_10" title="Pioneer 10">
           Pioneer 10
          </a>
          captured in 1973 the first closeup images of Europa – however the probe was too far away to obtain more detailed images
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px">
         <div class="thumbimage">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Europa_-_July_9_1979_(18267960842).jpg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="992" data-file-width="1759" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Europa_-_July_9_1979_%2818267960842%29.jpg/220px-Europa_-_July_9_1979_%2818267960842%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Europa_-_July_9_1979_%2818267960842%29.jpg/330px-Europa_-_July_9_1979_%2818267960842%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Europa_-_July_9_1979_%2818267960842%29.jpg/440px-Europa_-_July_9_1979_%2818267960842%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
          </a>
         </div>
         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
          Europa seen in detail in 1979 by
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Voyager_2" title="Voyager 2">
            Voyager 2
           </a>
          </i>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Exploration of Europa began with the Jupiter flybys of
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Pioneer_10" title="Pioneer 10">
         Pioneer 10
        </a>
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Pioneer_11" title="Pioneer 11">
         11
        </a>
       </i>
       in 1973 and 1974 respectively. The first closeup photos were of low resolution compared to later missions. The two
       <a href="/wiki/Voyager_program" title="Voyager program">
        Voyager
       </a>
       probes traveled through the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jovian_system" title="Jovian system">
        Jovian system
       </a>
       in 1979, providing more-detailed images of Europa's icy surface. The images caused many scientists to speculate about the possibility of a liquid ocean underneath. Starting in 1995, the
       <a href="/wiki/Galileo_(spacecraft)" title="Galileo (spacecraft)">
        <i>
         Galileo
        </i>
        spaceprobe
       </a>
       orbited Jupiter for eight years, until 2003, and provided the most detailed examination of the
       <a href="/wiki/Galilean_moons" title="Galilean moons">
        Galilean moons
       </a>
       to date. It included the "Galileo Europa Mission" and "Galileo Millennium Mission", with numerous close flybys of Europa.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">
        <a href="#cite_note-112">
         [106]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2007,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/New_Horizons" title="New Horizons">
         New Horizons
        </a>
       </i>
       imaged Europa, as it flew by the Jovian system while on its way to
       <a href="/wiki/Pluto" title="Pluto">
        Pluto
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113">
        <a href="#cite_note-113">
         [107]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Future_missions">
        Future missions
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Europa_(moon)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Future missions">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Conjectures regarding
       <a href="/wiki/Extraterrestrial_life" title="Extraterrestrial life">
        extraterrestrial life
       </a>
       have ensured a high-profile for Europa and have led to steady lobbying for future missions.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europabudget_114-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Europabudget-114">
         [108]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PlanetarySocEuropa_115-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-PlanetarySocEuropa-115">
         [109]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The aims of these missions have ranged from examining Europa's chemical composition to searching for extraterrestrial life in its hypothesized subsurface oceans.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EuropaLife_116-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-EuropaLife-116">
         [110]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Muir2002_117-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Muir2002-117">
         [111]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Robotic missions to Europa need to endure the high-radiation environment around itself and Jupiter.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PlanetarySocEuropa_115-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-PlanetarySocEuropa-115">
         [109]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Europa receives about 5.40
       <a href="/wiki/Sievert" title="Sievert">
        Sv
       </a>
       of radiation per day.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ringwald2000_118-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Ringwald2000-118">
         [112]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2011, a Europa mission was recommended by the U.S.
       <a href="/wiki/Planetary_Science_Decadal_Survey" title="Planetary Science Decadal Survey">
        Planetary Science Decadal Survey
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zab_119-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-zab-119">
         [113]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In response, NASA commissioned Europa lander concept studies in 2011, along with concepts for a Europa flyby (
       <i>
        Europa Clipper
       </i>
       ), and a Europa orbiter.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">
        <a href="#cite_note-120">
         [114]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">
        <a href="#cite_note-121">
         [115]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The orbiter element option concentrates on the "ocean" science, while the multiple-flyby element (
       <i>
        Clipper
       </i>
       ) concentrates on the chemistry and energy science. On 13 January 2014, the House Appropriations Committee announced a new bipartisan bill that includes $80 million funding to continue the Europa mission concept studies.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">
        <a href="#cite_note-122">
         [116]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">
        <a href="#cite_note-123">
         [117]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        In 2012,
        <i>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jupiter_Icy_Moon_Explorer" title="Jupiter Icy Moon Explorer">
          Jupiter Icy Moon Explorer
         </a>
        </i>
        (JUICE) was selected by the European Space Agency (
        <a href="/wiki/European_Space_Agency" title="European Space Agency">
         ESA
        </a>
        ) as a planned mission.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-selection_24-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-selection-24">
          [18]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-l1_124-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-l1-124">
          [118]
         </a>
        </sup>
        That mission includes 2 flybys of Europa, but is more focused on
        <a href="/wiki/Ganymede_(moon)" title="Ganymede (moon)">
         Ganymede
        </a>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-juice-objectives_125-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-juice-objectives-125">
          [119]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Europa_Clipper" title="Europa Clipper">
          Europa Clipper
         </a>
        </i>
        — In July 2013 an updated concept for a flyby Europa mission called
        <i>
         Europa Clipper
        </i>
        was presented by the
        <a href="/wiki/Jet_Propulsion_Laboratory" title="Jet Propulsion Laboratory">
         Jet Propulsion Laboratory
        </a>
        (JPL) and the
        <a href="/wiki/Applied_Physics_Laboratory" title="Applied Physics Laboratory">
         Applied Physics Laboratory
        </a>
        (APL).
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126">
         <a href="#cite_note-126">
          [120]
         </a>
        </sup>
        In May 2015, NASA announced that it had accepted development of the
        <i>
         Europa Clipper
        </i>
        mission, and revealed the instruments it will use.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EuropaClipperAnnounce_127-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-EuropaClipperAnnounce-127">
          [121]
         </a>
        </sup>
        The aim of
        <i>
         Europa Clipper
        </i>
        is to explore Europa in order to investigate its
        <a href="/wiki/Planetary_habitability" title="Planetary habitability">
         habitability
        </a>
        , and to aid selecting sites for a future lander. The
        <i>
         Europa Clipper
        </i>
        would not orbit Europa, but instead orbit Jupiter and conduct 45 low-altitude
        <a href="/wiki/Planetary_flyby" title="Planetary flyby">
         flybys
        </a>
        of Europa during its envisioned mission. The probe would carry an ice-penetrating radar, short-wave infrared spectrometer, topographical imager, and an ion- and neutral-mass spectrometer.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Europa_Lander_(NASA)" title="Europa Lander (NASA)">
         Europa Lander (NASA)
        </a>
        is a recent concept mission under study.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Old_proposals">
        Old proposals
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Europa_(moon)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Old proposals">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:406px;max-width:406px">
        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:184px;max-width:184px">
         <div class="thumbimage">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cryobot.jpg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="610" data-file-width="768" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Cryobot.jpg/182px-Cryobot.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Cryobot.jpg/273px-Cryobot.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Cryobot.jpg/364px-Cryobot.jpg 2x" width="182"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:218px;max-width:218px">
         <div class="thumbimage">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:JIMO_Europa_Lander_Mission.jpg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="661" data-file-width="983" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/JIMO_Europa_Lander_Mission.jpg/216px-JIMO_Europa_Lander_Mission.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/JIMO_Europa_Lander_Mission.jpg/324px-JIMO_Europa_Lander_Mission.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/JIMO_Europa_Lander_Mission.jpg/432px-JIMO_Europa_Lander_Mission.jpg 2x" width="216"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div style="clear:left">
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">
         <i>
          Left:
         </i>
         artist's concept of the
         <a href="/wiki/Cryobot" title="Cryobot">
          cryobot
         </a>
         and its deployed 'hydrobot' submersible.
         <i>
          Right:
         </i>
         Europa Lander Mission concept, NASA 2005
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128">
          <a href="#cite_note-128">
           [122]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In the early 2000s,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Jupiter_Europa_Orbiter" title="Jupiter Europa Orbiter">
         Jupiter Europa Orbiter
        </a>
       </i>
       led by NASA and the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Jupiter_Ganymede_Orbiter" title="Jupiter Ganymede Orbiter">
         Jupiter Ganymede Orbiter
        </a>
       </i>
       led by the ESA were proposed together as an
       <a href="/wiki/Outer_Planet_Flagship_Mission" title="Outer Planet Flagship Mission">
        Outer Planet Flagship Mission
       </a>
       to Jupiter's icy moons called
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Europa_Jupiter_System_Mission" title="Europa Jupiter System Mission">
        Europa Jupiter System Mission
       </a>
       , with a planned launch in 2020.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA2009_129-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-NASA2009-129">
         [123]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2009 it was given priority over
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Titan_Saturn_System_Mission" title="Titan Saturn System Mission">
         Titan Saturn System Mission
        </a>
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rincon2009_130-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Rincon2009-130">
         [124]
        </a>
       </sup>
       At that time, there was competition from other proposals.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ESA2007_131-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ESA2007-131">
         [125]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/JAXA" title="JAXA">
        Japan
       </a>
       proposed
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Jupiter_Magnetospheric_Orbiter" title="Jupiter Magnetospheric Orbiter">
         Jupiter Magnetospheric Orbiter
        </a>
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Jovian_Europa_Orbiter" title="Jovian Europa Orbiter">
         Jovian Europa Orbiter
        </a>
       </i>
       was an ESA Cosmic Vision concept study from 2007. Another concept was
       <i>
        Ice Clipper
       </i>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McKay2002_132-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-McKay2002-132">
         [126]
        </a>
       </sup>
       which would have used an impactor similar to the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Deep_Impact_(spacecraft)" title="Deep Impact (spacecraft)">
         Deep Impact
        </a>
       </i>
       mission—it would make a controlled crash into the surface of Europa, generating a plume of debris that would then be collected by a small spacecraft flying through the plume.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McKay2002_132-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-McKay2002-132">
         [126]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Goodman1998_133-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Goodman1998-133">
         [127]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Jupiter_Icy_Moons_Orbiter" title="Jupiter Icy Moons Orbiter">
         Jupiter Icy Moons Orbiter
        </a>
       </i>
       (JIMO) was a partially developed fission-powered spacecraft with ion thrusters that was cancelled in 2006.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PlanetarySocEuropa_115-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-PlanetarySocEuropa-115">
         [109]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Budget_134-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Budget-134">
         [128]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It was part of
       <a href="/wiki/Project_Prometheus" title="Project Prometheus">
        Project Prometheus
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Budget_134-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Budget-134">
         [128]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <i>
        Europa Lander Mission
       </i>
       proposed a small nuclear-powered Europa lander for JIMO.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-elm_135-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-elm-135">
         [129]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It would travel with the orbiter, which would also function as a communication relay to Earth.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-elm_135-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-elm-135">
         [129]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Europa_Orbiter" title="Europa Orbiter">
         Europa Orbiter
        </a>
       </i>
       — Its objective would be to characterize the extent of the ocean and its relation to the deeper interior. Instrument payload could include a radio subsystem,
       <a href="/wiki/Lidar" title="Lidar">
        laser altimeter
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Magnetometer" title="Magnetometer">
        magnetometer
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Langmuir_probe" title="Langmuir probe">
        Langmuir probe
       </a>
       , and a mapping camera.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136">
        <a href="#cite_note-136">
         [130]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137">
        <a href="#cite_note-137">
         [131]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <i>
        Europa Orbiter
       </i>
       received a go-ahead in 1999 but was canceled in 2002. This orbiter featured a special ice-penetrating radar that would allow it to scan below the surface.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-waterworld_41-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-waterworld-41">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       More ambitious ideas have been put forward including an impactor in combination with a thermal drill to search for
       <a href="/wiki/Biosignature" title="Biosignature">
        biosignatures
       </a>
       that might be frozen in the shallow subsurface.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weiss2010_138-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Weiss2010-138">
         [132]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Thermal_139-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Thermal-139">
         [133]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Another proposal put forward in 2001 calls for a large
       <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power" title="Nuclear power">
        nuclear-powered
       </a>
       "melt probe" (
       <a href="/wiki/Cryobot" title="Cryobot">
        cryobot
       </a>
       ) that would melt through the ice until it reached an ocean below.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PlanetarySocEuropa_115-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-PlanetarySocEuropa-115">
         [109]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Knight2002_140-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Knight2002-140">
         [134]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Once it reached the water, it would deploy an autonomous underwater vehicle (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AUV" title="AUV">
        hydrobot
       </a>
       ) that would gather information and send it back to Earth.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bridges2000_141-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Bridges2000-141">
         [135]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Both the cryobot and the hydrobot would have to undergo some form of extreme sterilization to prevent detection of Earth organisms instead of native life and to prevent
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Forward-contamination" title="Forward-contamination">
        contamination
       </a>
       of the subsurface ocean.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASSSB_142-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-NASSSB-142">
         [136]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This suggested approach has not yet reached a formal conceptual planning stage.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Powell2005_143-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Powell2005-143">
         [137]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Habitability_potential">
        Habitability potential
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Europa_(moon)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Habitability potential">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Blacksmoker_in_Atlantic_Ocean.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1780" data-file-width="1208" height="250" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Blacksmoker_in_Atlantic_Ocean.jpg/170px-Blacksmoker_in_Atlantic_Ocean.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Blacksmoker_in_Atlantic_Ocean.jpg/255px-Blacksmoker_in_Atlantic_Ocean.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Blacksmoker_in_Atlantic_Ocean.jpg/340px-Blacksmoker_in_Atlantic_Ocean.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Blacksmoker_in_Atlantic_Ocean.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_smoker" title="Black smoker">
          black smoker
         </a>
         in the
         <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">
          Atlantic Ocean
         </a>
         . Driven by geothermal energy, this and
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lost_City_(hydrothermal_field)" title="Lost City (hydrothermal field)">
          other types
         </a>
         of hydrothermal vents create
         <a href="/wiki/Chemical_equilibrium" title="Chemical equilibrium">
          chemical disequilibria
         </a>
         that can provide energy sources for life.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       So far, there is no evidence that life exists on Europa, but Europa has emerged as one of the most likely locations in the Solar System for
       <a href="/wiki/Planetary_habitability" title="Planetary habitability">
        potential habitability
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ChemDisequilib_110-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-ChemDisequilib-110">
         [104]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schulze-Makuch2001_144-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Schulze-Makuch2001-144">
         [138]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Extraterrestrial_life" title="Extraterrestrial life">
        Life
       </a>
       could exist in its under-ice ocean, perhaps in an environment similar to Earth's deep-ocean
       <a href="/wiki/Hydrothermal_vent" title="Hydrothermal vent">
        hydrothermal vents
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EuropaLife_116-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-EuropaLife-116">
         [110]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jones2001_145-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Jones2001-145">
         [139]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Even if Europa lacks volcanic hydrothermal activity, a 2016 NASA study found that Earth-like levels of hydrogen and oxygen could be produced through processes related to
       <a href="/wiki/Serpentinite" title="Serpentinite">
        serpentinization
       </a>
       and ice-derived oxidants, which do not directly involve
       <a href="/wiki/Volcanism" title="Volcanism">
        volcanism
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jpl_2016-05-18_146-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-jpl_2016-05-18-146">
         [140]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2015, scientists announced that salt from a
       <a href="/wiki/Extraterrestrial_liquid_water" title="Extraterrestrial liquid water">
        subsurface ocean
       </a>
       may likely be coating some geological features on Europa, suggesting that the ocean is interacting with the seafloor. This may be important in determining if Europa could be habitable.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-20150512_22-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-NASA-20150512-22">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147">
        <a href="#cite_note-147">
         [141]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The likely presence of liquid water in contact with Europa's rocky
       <a href="/wiki/Mantle_(geology)" title="Mantle (geology)">
        mantle
       </a>
       has spurred calls to send a probe there.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Phillips2006_148-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Phillips2006-148">
         [142]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The energy provided by
       <a href="/wiki/Tidal_force" title="Tidal force">
        tidal flexing
       </a>
       drives active geological processes within Europa's interior, just as they do to a far more obvious degree on its sister moon
       <a href="/wiki/Io_(moon)" title="Io (moon)">
        Io
       </a>
       . Although Europa, like the Earth, may possess an internal energy source from radioactive decay, the energy generated by tidal flexing would be several orders of magnitude greater than any radiological source.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wilson2007_149-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Wilson2007-149">
         [143]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Life on Europa could exist clustered around hydrothermal vents on the ocean floor, or below the ocean floor, where
       <a href="/wiki/Endolith" title="Endolith">
        endoliths
       </a>
       are known to inhabit on Earth. Alternatively, it could exist clinging to the lower surface of Europa's ice layer, much like algae and bacteria in Earth's polar regions, or float freely in Europa's ocean.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-limit_150-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-limit-150">
         [144]
        </a>
       </sup>
       If Europa's ocean is too cold, biological processes similar to those known on Earth could not take place. If it is too salty, only extreme
       <a href="/wiki/Halophile" title="Halophile">
        halophiles
       </a>
       could survive in that environment.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-limit_150-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-limit-150">
         [144]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2010, a model proposed by Richard Greenberg of the University of Arizona proposed that irradiation of ice on Europa's surface could saturate its crust with oxygen and peroxide, which could then be transported via tectonic processes into the interior ocean. Such a process could render Europa's ocean as oxygenated as our own within just 12 million years, allowing for the existence of complex, multicellular lifeforms.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151">
        <a href="#cite_note-151">
         [145]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Evidence suggests the existence of lakes of liquid water entirely encased in Europa's icy outer shell and distinct from a liquid ocean thought to exist farther down beneath the ice shell.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-europagreatlake_59-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-europagreatlake-59">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-europagreatlakeairhart_60-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-europagreatlakeairhart-60">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
       If confirmed, the lakes could be yet another potential habitat for life.
      </p>
      <p>
       Evidence suggests that
       <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen_peroxide" title="Hydrogen peroxide">
        hydrogen peroxide
       </a>
       is abundant across much of the surface of Europa.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152">
        <a href="#cite_note-152">
         [146]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Because hydrogen peroxide decays into oxygen and water when combined with liquid water, the authors argue that it could be an important energy supply for simple life forms.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Clay_minerals" title="Clay minerals">
        Clay-like minerals
       </a>
       (specifically,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Phyllosilicates" title="Phyllosilicates">
        phyllosilicates
       </a>
       ), often associated with
       <a href="/wiki/Organic_matter" title="Organic matter">
        organic matter
       </a>
       on Earth, have been detected on the icy crust of Europa.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-20131211_153-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-NASA-20131211-153">
         [147]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The presence of the minerals may have been the result of a collision with an
       <a href="/wiki/Asteroid" title="Asteroid">
        asteroid
       </a>
       or
       <a href="/wiki/Comet" title="Comet">
        comet
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NASA-20131211_153-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-NASA-20131211-153">
         [147]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Some scientists have speculated that life on Earth could have been blasted into space by asteroid collisions and arrived on the moons of Jupiter in a process called
       <a href="/wiki/Panspermia#Lithopanspermia" title="Panspermia">
        lithopanspermia
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154">
        <a href="#cite_note-154">
         [148]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

           <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Astrobiology&amp;rft.atitle=Transport+Rates+of+Radiolytic+Substances+into+Europa%27s+Ocean%3A+Implications+for+the+Potential+Origin+and+Maintenance+of+Life&amp;rft.volume=10&amp;rft.issue=3&amp;rft.pages=275-283&amp;rft.date=2010-05&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1089%2Fast.2009.0386&amp;rft_id=info%3Abibcode%2F2010AsBio..10..275G&amp;rft.au=Richard+Greenberg&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEuropa+%28moon%29">
